  Output file: output/theory_demo_output.txt

  THEORY is an open-source alternative to enterprise TI platforms.
  It generates analyst-grade dossiers from multiple free sources:
  MITRE ATT&CK · Malpedia · AlienVault OTX · SigmaHQ · ThreatFox · CISA

$ /Users/terminal/theory/venv/bin/python theory.py --help

usage: theory [-h] [--actor NAME] [--sources SOURCE[,SOURCE...]]
              [--output FORMAT] [--no-save] [--verbose] [--list-sources]
              [--list-actors] [--update-bundles]

THEORY — open-source multi-source threat actor intelligence framework.
Generates analyst-grade dossiers from MITRE ATT&CK, Malpedia, OTX, Sigma, ThreatFox, and more.

options:
  -h, --help            show this help message and exit
  --actor, -a NAME      Threat actor name or any known alias. Examples:
                        "APT28", "Fancy Bear", "Cozy Bear", "Lazarus Group",
                        "Volt Typhoon". Use --list-actors to see all supported
                        actors and their aliases.
  --sources, -s SOURCE[,SOURCE...]
                        Comma-separated intelligence sources. Available:
                        mitre, cisa, malpedia, otx, sigma, threatfox. Default:
                        mitre,malpedia,otx. Use --list-sources for details on
                        each source.
  --output, -o FORMAT   Output format. dossier = terminal + markdown file
                        (default). json = raw profile JSON. stix = STIX 2.1
                        bundle for MISP/OpenCTI/Sentinel import. all = write
                        all three formats.
  --no-save             Print output to terminal only — do not write files to
                        output/dossiers/.
  --verbose, -v         Enable debug logging. Shows which sources are queried
                        and what data is returned.

information commands (no actor required):
  --list-sources        Show all available intelligence sources with auth
                        requirements and cache info.
  --list-actors         Show all actors with built-in cross-source alias
                        resolution.
  --update-bundles      Refresh the local ATT&CK STIX bundle and clear
                        Sigma/ThreatFox caches. Run periodically to stay
                        current with new ATT&CK releases and Sigma rules.

examples:
  python theory.py --actor APT28
  python theory.py --actor "Fancy Bear" --sources mitre,malpedia,otx
  python theory.py --actor Lazarus --sources mitre,malpedia,otx,sigma,threatfox
  python theory.py --actor APT41 --sources mitre,otx --output stix
  python theory.py --actor Turla --sources mitre,malpedia --output all
  python theory.py --actor APT29 --sources mitre --no-save
  python theory.py --list-sources
  python theory.py --list-actors
  python theory.py --update-bundles

notes:
  - --actor accepts any name or alias (e.g. "Cozy Bear" = APT29 = Midnight Blizzard)
  - Run --update-bundles periodically to refresh ATT&CK data and Sigma rules
  - First run with --sources sigma takes ~10 min to build the cache (instant after)
  - Set OTX_API_KEY and GITHUB_TOKEN in .env for best results
  - Output files are saved to output/dossiers/

      "description": "Adversaries may use a single or small list of commonly used passwords against many different accounts to attempt to acquire valid account credentials.     {
      "technique_id": "T1598",
      "name": "Phishing for Information",
      "tactic": "Reconnaissance",
      "description": "Adversaries may send phishing messages to elicit sensitive information that can be used during targeting. Phishing for information is an attempt to trick targets into divulging information, frequently credentials or other actionable information.
